## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard modeling object in chemical kinetics. With only (t, A) available, the task most likely seeks a classical rate-law ODE structure where the reaction rate depends on concentration (reaction order, saturation, autocatalysis) and possibly explicit time-variation (activation/deactivation, forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A over the operating range)
- First-order decay (unimolecular): dA_dt = -c0 * A (elementary first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay (bimolecular/self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to A squared)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/overall reaction order c1)
- Linear relaxation to steady state (CSTR/approach to equilibrium proxy): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (A approaches level c1 with rate c0)
- Reversible first-order approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) - c2 * A (net of forward/backward first-order terms)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating then self-limiting growth/consumption)
- Gompertz-type kinetics (asymmetric saturation): dA_dt = c0 * A * log(c1 / A) (slow start then rapid change then saturation)
- Saturating/inhibited rate (rational form): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (effective rate saturates at large A)
- Substrate-inhibition-like rational: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A**2 + c1 * A + c2) (rate decreases at high A due to self-inhibition/complexation)
- Time-varying first-order rate constant (deactivation/aging): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective k(t) decays with time)
- Induction/activation transient: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (k(t) ramps up from 0 to c0)
- Oscillatory forcing/photokinetics proxy: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (periodically modulated rate constant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If A decays exponentially in time, the underlying structure is typically dA_dt proportional to A (first-order term -c*A).
- If the rate accelerates strongly at higher concentration, include higher-order powers A**n (n>1) to represent bimolecular/chain-branching-like dependence.
- If A approaches a nonzero plateau, use a driving term toward a setpoint (c1 - A) rather than pure decay.
- If there is a clear equilibrium level with opposing processes, represent forward/backward contributions as separate linear terms in A and (c1 - A).
- If the rate initially increases with A but later diminishes (self-limitation), use autocatalytic factors like A*(c1 - A) or A*log(c1/A).
- If the rate increases with A at low A but saturates at high A, prefer rational forms such as A/(A+c1) multiplying a maximum rate.
- If the process slows down over time even at the same A (e.g., catalyst deactivation), multiply a concentration-dependent rate by exp(-c*t).
- If there is an induction period (rate starts near zero and turns on), multiply by (1 - exp(-c*t)) to model ramp-up.
- If external conditions vary periodically (e.g., light intensity cycling), allow sinusoidal modulation of an effective rate constant: (1 + c*sin(c*t)).
